Damage caused by storm of September 9, 1919, Havana					Written on verso: "View of the driveway connecting Havana and Vedado showing huge portions of the new concrete seawall broken up by the waves during the storm on Sept. 9th, 1919. They were carried entirely across the new boulevard being constructed along the seawall, then over the double street car track and finally deposited in the middle of the roadway at the foot of Santa Clara battery, as shown. These blocks were so large and heavy that it was necessary to blast them into smaller sections for removal.  The rough slabs in the foreground are pieces of the concrete base of the new boulevard mentioned above." "Photo by Harris Bros., Co., O'Reilly 104, Havana, Cuba." Also: "Used 1919." Disappearing River at San Antonio de los Baños, Artemisa					Written on verso: "A Disappearing River at San Antonio de los Baños . . . Once made the old town famous as a bathing resort takes a plunge into a black cavern and disappears from sight.  It is needless to say that the bathing was done at a respectful distance from this dark abyss. To keep the unwary traveller from stepping off the brink, a neat stone wall has been erected. San Antonio is one of the most interesting of the old inland towns and the tourist will do well to make it a visit if only to see this freak of nature.  Some sixty miles South a small stream makes its appearance from a rocky hillside said to be at least a part of this river but this has not been proven." Old church at San Antonio de los Baños, Artemisa					Written on front: "San Antonio de los Baños." Written on verso: "Old church at San Antonio de los Banos. The old Spanish churches of Cuba form one of the most interesting features to the tourist. Most of them equal in antiquity the California Missions of which so much has been written and these old buildings have in many cases fully as interesting features and histories. This church faces a pretty park full of flowers and shrubbery and at the time our picture was made school was being conducted inside. This was the real Cuban variety where each student studies aloud at the top of their voices making a veritable bedlam to stronger ears."  Stamp on verso: "Munson Steamship Line." Model of monument dedicated to General Máximo Gómez					Scale model of monument dedicated to General Máximo Gómez (1836-1905). This model was the winner of a design competition held from 1918 to 1919. The monument was not dedicated until 1935. Written on verso: "Model submitted by the Italian sculptor, Aldo Gamba, which won first prize of. . . In a world-wide competition for a monument to be erected in the memory of General Máximo Gómez in Colón Park, Havana, Cuba. Grupo San Juan Bautista De La Salle	San Juan Bautista De La Salle Group				La Federación de la Juventud Católica fue fundada el 11 de febrero de 1928 por el Hno. Victorino de la Congregación de los Hermanos De La Salle, con delegados de distintos colegios católicos de La Habana. En 1936 se reorganizó, cerrando distintos grupos, que fueron multiplicándose por todo el territorio nacional. El primer grupo que se creó en ese año fue el Grupo San Juan Bautista De La Salle, constituido en su mayoría por estudiantes unversitarios que aparecen en esta fotografía.
